# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Objective

Analyze the changes between Terraform v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 and produce a comprehensive migration guide for users upgrading from v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Terraform codebase:
- **v1.9.0**: implemented in `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/` (commit 7637a92)
- **v1.10.0**: implemented in `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/` (commit 24236f4)

Your task is to identify breaking changes and behavioral changes that affect users, then document migration steps.

## Required Analysis

Your migration guide must cover:

1. **S3 Backend Changes**
   - Removal of deprecated IAM role assumption attributes
   - Migration to `assume_role` block syntax
   - New S3 native state locking support

2. **Moved Blocks Syntax Changes**
   - New requirement to prepend `resource.` identifier when referencing resources with type names matching top-level blocks/keywords
   - Impact on existing `moved` blocks in configurations

3. **Sensitive Value Handling**
   - Changes to mark propagation in conditional expressions
   - When sensitive marks are now preserved (previously lost)
   - How to use `nonsensitive()` to override when needed

4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** (new feature with migration implications)
   - Introduction of ephemeral input variables and outputs
   - New ephemeral resource mode
   - Impact on secret handling in state files

## Expected Output

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` with the following structure:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the upgrade and major themes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Each breaking change with:
   - What changed and why
   - Before/after code examples
   - Step-by-step migration instructions
   - Common pitfalls to avoid
3. **New Features with Migration Impact** - Features that change how users should write Terraform
4. **Testing Your Migration** - How to validate the upgrade was successful
5. **Rollback Guidance** - How to safely rollback if needed

## Evaluation

Your review will be evaluated on detection accuracy and fix quality.

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changes in specific files
- Look for UPGRADE notes in release documentation
- Examine test files to understand behavioral changes
- Check for deprecation warnings and removed features
- Pay attention to changes in internal/backend/remote-state/s3/, internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract.go, and lang/marks/ directories

Good luck!


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

   - Common resource types affected
   - Step-by-step validation process

Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\\n24: \\n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n26: \\n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\\n39: \\n40: ## Previous Releases\\n41: \\n42: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n43: \\n44: - [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\\n45: - [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\\n46: - [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\\n47: - [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\\n48: - [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\\n49: - [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\\n50: - [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\\n51: - [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\\n52: - [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\\n53: - [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\\n54: - [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\\n55: - [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\\n56: - [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\\n57: - [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\\n58: - [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\\n59: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/CHANGELOG.md%3FL1-100\"}",
  "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: ## 1.10.0 (November 27, 2024)\n2: \n3: NEW FEATURES:\n4:  - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\n7: \n8: BUG FIXES:\n9: \n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\n24: \n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\n26: \n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\n32: \n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\n34: \n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. If specified, enables the machine readable JSON output. ([#34886](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/34886))\\n14: * `terraform test`: Test runs can now pass sensitive values to input variables while preserving their dynamic sensitivity. Previously sensitivity would be preserved only for variables statically declared as being sensitive, using `sensitive = true`. ([#35021](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35021))\\n15: * config: Input variable validation rules can now refer to other objects in the same module. ([#35088](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35088))\\n18: * built-in `terraform` provider: Allows `moved` block refactoring from the `hashicorp/null` provider `null_resource` resource type to the `terraform_data` resource type. ([#35163](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35163))\\n19: * `terraform output` with `cloud` block: Terraform no longer suggests that data loss could occur when outputs are not available. ([#34822](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/34822))\\n21:     If an entered line contains opening parentheses/etc that are not closed, Terraform will await another line of input to complete the expression. This initial implementation is primarily intended to support pasting in multi-line expressions from elsewhere, rather than for manual multi-line editing, so the interactive editing support is currently limited.\\n22: * cli: Reduced copying of state to improve performance with large numbers of resources. ([#35164](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35164))\\n23: * `removed` blocks can now declare destroy-time provisioners which will be executed when the associated resource instances are destroyed. ([#34387](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34387))\\n29: * `terraform test`: Fix bug in which non-Hashicorp providers required by testing modules and initialised within the test files were assigned incorrect registry addresses. ([#35161](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35161))\\n30: * config: The `templatefile` function no longer returns a \\\"panic\\\" error if the template file path is marked as sensitive. Instead, the template rendering result is also marked as sensitive. ([#35180](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35180))\\n31: * config: `import` blocks which referenced resources in non-existent modules were silently ignored when they should have raised an error ([#35330](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35330))\\n32: * `terraform init`: When selecting a version for a provider that has both positive and negative version constraints for the same prerelease -- e.g. `1.2.0-beta.1, !1.2.0-beta.1` -- the negative constraint will now overrule the positive, for consistency with how negative constraints are handled otherwise. Previously Terraform would incorrectly treat the positive as overriding the negative if the specified version was a prerelease. If you encounter any problems during upgrading which are not\\n20: covered this guide, please start a new topic in\\n21: [the Terraform community forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\\n22: to discuss it.\\n23: \\n24: ## Conflicting `moved` block references\\n25: \\n26: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords such as `local`, `each`, `self` etc. when parsing resource addresses.\\n27: Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and\\n28: keywords from moved blocks will need to prepend the reference identifier with `resource.`.\\n29: \\n30: ## S3 Backend \\n31: \\n32: ### S3 Native State Locking\\n33: \\n34: The S3 backend now supports S3 native state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature.\\n35: An S3 lock can be used alongside a DynamoDB lock, or independently.\\n36: When both locking mechanisms are configured, a lock must be successfully acquired from both locations before subsequent operations will proceed.\\n37: \\n38: To opt-in to S3 native state locking, set `use_lockfile` to `true`.\\n39: \\n40: ```terraform\\n41: terraform {\\n42:   backend \\\"s3\\\" {\\n43:     # additional configuration omitted for brevity\\n44:     use_lockfile = true\\n45:   }\\n46: }\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: With S3 locking enabled, a lock file will be placed in the same location as the state file.\\n50: The lock file will be named identically to the state file, but with a `.tflock` extension.\\n51: **S3 bucket policies and IAM policies attached to the calling principal may need to be adjusted to include permissions for the new lock file.**\\n52: \\n53: In a future minor version of Terraform the experimental label will be removed from the `use_lockfile` attribute and attributes related to DynamoDB based locking will be deprecated.\\n54: \\n55: ### Root Assume Role Attribute Removal\\n56: \\n57: Several root level attributes related to IAM role assumption which were previously deprecated have been removed.\\n58: Each removed field has an analogous field inside the [`assume_role` block](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3#assume-role-configuration) which should be used instead.\\n59: \\n60: | Removed | Replacement |\\n61: | --- | --- |\\n62: | `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\\n63: | `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\\n64: | `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\\n65: | `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\\n66: | `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\\n67: | `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |\\n68: | `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\\n69: | `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\\n70: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/website/docs/language/upgrade-guides/index.mdx%3FL1-150\"}",

{
  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release that introduces new features for managing ephemeral data and contains important breaking changes that require attention when upgrading.\n\nThis guide covers the key breaking changes and new features you need to be aware of when migrating from Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.\n\n### Major Themes\n\n1. **Ephemeral Values and Resources** - New capability to handle sensitive data without persisting it to state\n2. **S3 Backend Restructuring** - Removal of deprecated IAM role assumption attributes\n3. **Improved Sensitive Value Handling** - Better consistency in mark propagation across conditional expressions\n4. **Moved Block Keyword Safety** - Improved resource addressing to avoid conflicts with reserved keywords\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 removes the following deprecated root-level attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes must now be specified within the `assume_role` block.\n\n| Removed Attribute | New Location |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe consolidation into the `assume_role` block provides better organization and makes the configuration structure more consistent with Terraform's block-based syntax patterns.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-bucket\"\n    key               = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Deprecated attributes at root level\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/MyRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                  = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy           = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags             = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-bucket\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # New assume_role block structure\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn             = \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/MyRole\"\n      session_name         = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id          = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration             = 3600\n      policy               = jsonencode({...})\n      tags                 = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Locate your S3 backend configuration** - Find the `terraform` block with `backend \"s3\"` in your root module (typically in `main.tf` or a dedicated `backend.tf`)\n\n2. **Create the `assume_role` block** - If you don't have one, add an empty `assume_role { }` block\n\n3. **Move deprecated attributes** - Move each deprecated attribute inside the `assume_role` block, using the new attribute names (e.g., `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration`)\n\n4. **Remove old attributes** - Delete the deprecated root-level attributes\n\n5. **Validate the configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure the syntax is correct\n\n6. **Plan before applying** - Run `terraform plan` to ensure no state changes are planned before applying\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting to rename duration attributes** - Remember that `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration` (without the `assume_role_` prefix and `_seconds` suffix)\n- **Mixing old and new attributes** - Don't use both old root-level attributes and new block attributes simultaneously\n- **Case sensitivity** - Ensure you use the exact attribute names (e.g., `duration`, not `duration_seconds`)\n- **WebIdentity configuration** - If you use `assume_role_with_web_identity`, that block remains separate from `assume_role` and doesn't change\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces experimental S3-native state locking as an opt-in feature. You can now use S3 Object Lock for state file locking instead of (or in addition to) DynamoDB.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nS3-native locking reduces dependencies on external services and integrates better with organizations that already rely on S3 bucket policies and object lock configurations.\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- This feature is **experimental** and subject to change\n- When enabled, S3 locks are acquired **alongside** DynamoDB locks if both are configured\n- **Both locks must be successfully acquired** before operations proceed\n- S3 bucket and IAM policies need to be updated to allow the application to manage `.tflock` files\n\n#### Enabling S3 Native State Locking\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-bucket\"\n    key               = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable experimental S3 native locking\n    use_lockfile = true\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### S3 Bucket Policy Update Required\n\nWhen enabling `use_lockfile = true`, the lock file is stored alongside the state file with a `.tflock` extension. Update your bucket policy:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/TerraformRole\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/terraform.tfstate*\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/TerraformRole\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:ListBucket\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review your current locking setup** - Determine if you're using DynamoDB, S3-native, or no locking\n2. **Update bucket policies** - Add permissions for `.tflock` files if enabling S3 locking\n3. **Test in a non-production environment first** - Verify the configuration works before applying to production\n4. **Plan the transition** - If migrating from DynamoDB-only to dual locking, plan for the brief period where both are active\n5. **Monitor lock acquisition** - Watch logs to ensure locks are properly acquired from both sources\n\n#### Future Deprecation Notice\n\nIn a future minor version of Terraform, DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated, and you'll need to migrate to S3-native locking or remove the DynamoDB configuration entirely.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Keyword Conflict Resolution\n\n#### What Changed\n\nMoved blocks now respect reserved keywords (`local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `data`, `resource`, `terraform`, `variable`, `output`, etc.) when parsing resource addresses.\n\nIf you reference a resource whose type name matches a reserved keyword, you must now prepend `resource.` to the identifier in `moved` blocks.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThis change prevents ambiguous resource references that could be interpreted as variable references or other language constructs. It ensures that moved blocks always reference the resource you intend.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nThis configuration would work if you had a resource type matching a keyword:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = output.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nYou must now use the `resource.` prefix for any resource type that matches a keyword:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.output.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n#### Resource Types That Require `resource.` Prefix\n\nThe following commonly-used providers have resource types that match reserved keywords:\n\n- `local_file` (type: `local`) - Actually safe, but ensure clarity\n- Custom providers with types named: `data`, `output`, `module`, `resource`, `variable`, `terraform`, `each`, `count`, `self`\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify moved blocks in your configuration** - Search for all `moved` blocks in your configuration\n\n2. **Check resource type names** - For each `moved` block, verify if the resource type name matches any reserved keyword\n\n3. **Identify problematic references** - Run `terraform init` and `terraform plan` to see if any moved blocks produce errors about conflicting keywords\n\n4. **Add `resource.` prefix** - For any problematic references, prepend `resource.` to the resource reference in the `moved` block\n\n5. **Validate the configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure all moved blocks are valid\n\n6. **Test the refactoring** - Apply the configuration to verify the moved blocks work correctly\n\n#### Common Examples\n\n**Example 1: Custom provider with resource type `local`**\n\n```hcl\n# v1.10.0 - If using a custom provider with \"local\" resource type\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n**Example 2: Normal resources (no change needed)**\n\n```hcl\n# These don't need changes - \"aws_instance\" and \"aws_security_group\"\n# don't match reserved keywords\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Not checking all moved blocks** - Search your entire codebase for moved blocks\n- **Forgetting about custom providers** - If you use custom providers, check their resource type names\n- **Applying prefix unnecessarily** - Only add `resource.` if the resource type actually conflicts with a keyword\n- **Ignoring error messages** - If Terraform reports a keyword conflict, add the prefix\n\n---\n\n## Sensitive Value Handling Improvements\n\n### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive marks are propagated in conditional expressions (`if/then/else`) and `for` expressions. In certain cases where v1.9.0 would lose sensitive marks, v1.10.0 preserves them for consistency.\n\n### Key Improvements\n\n1. **Conditional expressions now preserve sensitive marks** from all branches\n2. **For expressions preserve sensitive marks** when the result depends on sensitive inputs\n3. **Unknown values with sensitive marks** are now handled correctly\n4. **Bug fix: Incorrect transfer of sensitive marks** to nested resource values has been corrected\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThese changes typically **improve security** by ensuring sensitive values remain marked throughout evaluation. However, you may see new \"sensitive value\" warnings in outputs that were previously hidden.\n\n### Before (v1.9.0) vs After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\n# Example 1: Conditional expression with sensitive values\nvariable \"password\" {\n  sensitive = true\n  default   = \"secret\"\n}\n\nvariable \"use_custom\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\noutput \"chosen_password\" {\n  # In v1.9.0: This output might NOT be marked sensitive if use_custom is true\n  # In v1.10.0: This output IS marked sensitive because one branch contains sensitive data\n  value = var.use_custom ? \"custom-value\" : var.password\n}\n```\n\n### Migration Steps for Sensitive Value Changes\n\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** and review any new \"sensitive value\" annotations\n2. **Update outputs** - If outputs now show as sensitive and you want them public, use `nonsensitive()`\n3. **Review conditionals** - Check any `if/then/else` expressions that involve sensitive data\n4. **Use `nonsensitive()` carefully** - Only use this function if you've verified the value is safe to expose\n\n### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override\n\n```hcl\n# Example: Extract non-sensitive data from sensitive value\nvariable \"api_response\" {\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\noutput \"status_code\" {\n  # Extract just the status code, which is public information\n  value = nonsensitive(regexall(\"Status: (\\\\d+)\", var.api_response)[0][0])\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Implications\n\n### Ephemeral Values and Resources\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral values as a new capability for handling sensitive data that should not be persisted to state or plan files. This is a significant feature for secret management.\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values exist only during a Terraform operation and are **not written to state files or plan files**. They're useful for:\n- Short-lived tokens and credentials\n- Temporary secrets from external services\n- Data that's only needed during apply but shouldn't be stored\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral variable\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  # This variable won't be stored in state/plan files\n}\n\n# Use it in a provider configuration\nprovider \"example\" {\n  api_token = var.api_token\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs (in child modules)\n\n```hcl\n# In a child module, define an ephemeral output\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = aws_iam_session_token.example.token\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral resource (provider-dependent)\nephemeral \"vault_generic_secret\" \"database_credentials\" {\n  path = \"secret/data/database\"\n}\n\n# Use it in another resource\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"example\" {\n  master_password = ephemeral.vault_generic_secret.database_credentials.data[\"password\"]\n}\n```\n\n#### Important Restrictions\n\n- Ephemeral values can **only** be referenced in:\n  - Other ephemeral contexts\n  - Provider configurations\n  - Provisioner and connection blocks\n  - Other ephemeral variables/outputs/resources\n\n- **Cannot** be referenced in regular resources or outputs\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\nNew in v1.10.0, use this function to replace ephemeral values with null while preserving non-ephemeral values:\n\n```hcl\n# Convert ephemeral values to null before storing elsewhere\nlocal {\n  safe_for_storage = ephemeralasnull(var.api_token)\n}\n```\n\n#### When to Use Ephemeral Values\n\n- **Provider authentication** - Pass credentials without storing in state\n- **Temporary secrets** - Use short-lived tokens from secret backends\n- **Sensitive defaults** - Provide sensitive default values that shouldn't be persisted\n- **Module outputs** - Return credentials from child modules without state persistence\n\n#### When NOT to Use Ephemeral Values\n\n- Regular resource attributes (use `sensitive = true` instead)\n- Data that needs to persist across `terraform plan` and `terraform apply`\n- State that must be available in other Terraform operations\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Checklist\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n- [ ] Backup your current state file\n- [ ] Review and document all moved blocks in your configuration\n- [ ] Review S3 backend configuration for deprecated attributes\n- [ ] Check for any custom providers with resource type names matching keywords\n- [ ] Test upgrade in a non-production environment first\n\n### Validation Commands\n\n```bash\n# Initialize with the new version\nterraform init\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Plan to identify changes\nterraform plan -out=tfplan\n\n# Review the plan carefully\nterraform show tfplan\n\n# Apply only after reviewing\nterraform apply tfplan\n```\n\n### Key Validation Points\n\n1. **Moved blocks** - Verify no errors about keyword conflicts\n2. **S3 backend** - Confirm IAM role configuration is under the `assume_role` block\n3. **Sensitive values** - Check for any new \"sensitive value\" annotations\n4. **Plan result** - Ensure the plan shows no unexpected resource changes\n\n### Testing Sensitive Value Changes\n\n```bash\n# Run plan and grep for sensitive value indications\nterraform plan | grep -i sensitive\n\n# Compare before/after behavior with specific outputs\nterraform output -raw my_output  # Should fail if marked as sensitive\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If You Need to Rollback\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n1. **Revert your configuration changes** back to v1.9.0 syntax\n2. **Install Terraform v1.9.0**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform version  # Confirm you're on v1.10.0\n   # Download v1.9.0 from https://www.terraform.io/downloads\n   terraform version  # Confirm v1.9.0\n   ```\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** to reinitialize with v1.9.0\n4. **Verify no state changes** with `terraform plan`\n5. **Contact Terraform support** if you identify a bug\n\n### Safe Rollback Strategy\n\n```bash\n# Step 1: Backup current state\ncp terraform.tfstate terraform.tfstate.v110.bak\n\n# Step 2: Revert configuration to v1.9.0 format\ngit checkout main -- *.tf  # or manually revert\n\n# Step 3: Switch to v1.9.0\ntfswitch 1.9.0  # or similar version manager\n\n# Step 4: Initialize with v1.9.0\nterraform init\n\n# Step 5: Verify no unintended changes\nterraform plan\n\n# Step 6: Contact support if plan shows unexpected changes\n```\n\n---\n\n## Specific Migration Examples\n\n### Example 1: Complete S3 Backend Migration\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.9.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                       = \"terraform-state\"\n    key                          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                       = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table               = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-prod\"\n    external_id                  = \"abc123xyz\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-prod\"\n      external_id  = \"abc123xyz\"\n      duration     = 3600\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 2: Ephemeral Variable Usage\n\n```hcl\n# Provider configuration with ephemeral token\nvariable \"vault_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  default   = null\n}\n\nprovider \"vault\" {\n  address = \"https://vault.example.com\"\n  token   = var.vault_token\n}\n\n# Retrieve secrets using the ephemeral provider\ndata \"vault_generic_secret\" \"database\" {\n  path = \"secret/data/database\"\n}\n\n# Use secrets (but they won't be stored in state)\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"example\" {\n  master_username = data.vault_generic_secret.database.data[\"username\"]\n  master_password = data.vault_generic_secret.database.data[\"password\"]\n\n  # Note: These values ARE still stored in state as regular resource attributes\n  # Ephemeral only prevents the variable/data source from being persisted\n}\n```\n\n### Example 3: Moved Block with Keyword\n\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource with type \"local\" (hypothetically)\nresource \"random_pet\" \"pet\" {\n  keepers = {\n    example = \"value\"\n  }\n}\n\n# And previously had:\n# resource \"local\" \"old_name\" { }\n\n# In v1.10.0, update the moved block:\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = random_pet.pet\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Required Actions\n\n### Minimum Required Changes\n\n1. **S3 Backend Users**: Move IAM role attributes inside `assume_role` block\n2. **Moved Block Users**: Add `resource.` prefix if resource type matches keywords\n3. **All Users**: Run `terraform validate` and `terraform plan` before applying\n\n### Recommended Best Practices\n\n1. Use ephemeral variables for provider authentication instead of sensitive variables\n2. Review conditional expressions involving sensitive values\n3. Update bucket policies if enabling S3-native locking\n4. Document ephemeral value usage in module comments\n\n### Timeline for Deprecations\n\n- v1.10.0 (Nov 2024): IAM attributes removed, moved blocks require keyword safety, ephemeral values introduced\n- v1.11+ (Future): DynamoDB locking for S3 backend to be deprecated\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check the official Terraform upgrade guide** - https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/upgrade-guides\n2. **Review error messages** - Terraform provides clear guidance on what changed\n3. **Test in non-production** - Always validate changes before production\n4. **Community forum** - https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core\n5. **GitHub issues** - https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: File Locations and Examples\n\n### Important Configuration Files\n\n- **Backend configuration**: Usually `backend.tf` or in `terraform {}` block of `main.tf`\n- **Moved blocks**: Can be in any `.tf` file, often in a dedicated `moved.tf`\n- **Variables**: Usually `variables.tf` or `variables/*.tf`\n- **Outputs**: Usually `outputs.tf`\n\n### Full Example: Multi-file Migration\n\n**backend.tf:**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**main.tf:**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n  required_providers {\n    aws = {\n      source  = \"hashicorp/aws\"\n      version = \"~> 5.0\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region = \"us-east-1\"\n}\n\nresource \"aws_instance\" \"example\" {\n  ami           = \"ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0\"\n  instance_type = \"t2.micro\"\n}\n```\n\n**moved.tf:**\n```hcl\n# Updated for v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_name\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated**: November 2024\n**Terraform Versions**: v1.9.0 \u2192 v1.10.0\n**Status**: Complete for General Availability\n",

  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release that introduces new features for managing ephemeral data and contains important breaking changes that require attention when upgrading.\n\nThis guide covers the key breaking changes and new features you need to be aware of when migrating from Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.\n\n### Major Themes\n\n1. **Ephemeral Values and Resources** - New capability to handle sensitive data without persisting it to state\n2. **S3 Backend Restructuring** - Removal of deprecated IAM role assumption attributes\n3. **Improved Sensitive Value Handling** - Better consistency in mark propagation across conditional expressions\n4. **Moved Block Keyword Safety** - Improved resource addressing to avoid conflicts with reserved keywords\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 removes the following deprecated root-level attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes must now be specified within the `assume_role` block.\n\n| Removed Attribute | New Location |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe consolidation into the `assume_role` block provides better organization and makes the configuration structure more consistent with Terraform's block-based syntax patterns.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-bucket\"\n    key               = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Deprecated attributes at root level\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/MyRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                  = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy           = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags             = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-bucket\"\n    key    = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # New assume_role block structure\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn             = \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/MyRole\"\n      session_name         = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id          = \"unique-external-id\"\n      duration             = 3600\n      policy               = jsonencode({...})\n      tags                 = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Locate your S3 backend configuration** - Find the `terraform` block with `backend \"s3\"` in your root module (typically in `main.tf` or a dedicated `backend.tf`)\n\n2. **Create the `assume_role` block** - If you don't have one, add an empty `assume_role { }` block\n\n3. **Move deprecated attributes** - Move each deprecated attribute inside the `assume_role` block, using the new attribute names (e.g., `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration`)\n\n4. **Remove old attributes** - Delete the deprecated root-level attributes\n\n5. **Validate the configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure the syntax is correct\n\n6. **Plan before applying** - Run `terraform plan` to ensure no state changes are planned before applying\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Forgetting to rename duration attributes** - Remember that `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration` (without the `assume_role_` prefix and `_seconds` suffix)\n- **Mixing old and new attributes** - Don't use both old root-level attributes and new block attributes simultaneously\n- **Case sensitivity** - Ensure you use the exact attribute names (e.g., `duration`, not `duration_seconds`)\n- **WebIdentity configuration** - If you use `assume_role_with_web_identity`, that block remains separate from `assume_role` and doesn't change\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces experimental S3-native state locking as an opt-in feature. You can now use S3 Object Lock for state file locking instead of (or in addition to) DynamoDB.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nS3-native locking reduces dependencies on external services and integrates better with organizations that already rely on S3 bucket policies and object lock configurations.\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- This feature is **experimental** and subject to change\n- When enabled, S3 locks are acquired **alongside** DynamoDB locks if both are configured\n- **Both locks must be successfully acquired** before operations proceed\n- S3 bucket and IAM policies need to be updated to allow the application to manage `.tflock` files\n\n#### Enabling S3 Native State Locking\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-bucket\"\n    key               = \"terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable experimental S3 native locking\n    use_lockfile = true\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### S3 Bucket Policy Update Required\n\nWhen enabling `use_lockfile = true`, the lock file is stored alongside the state file with a `.tflock` extension. Update your bucket policy:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/TerraformRole\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/terraform.tfstate*\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::ACCOUNT_ID:role/TerraformRole\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:ListBucket\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review your current locking setup** - Determine if you're using DynamoDB, S3-native, or no locking\n2. **Update bucket policies** - Add permissions for `.tflock` files if enabling S3 locking\n3. **Test in a non-production environment first** - Verify the configuration works before applying to production\n4. **Plan the transition** - If migrating from DynamoDB-only to dual locking, plan for the brief period where both are active\n5. **Monitor lock acquisition** - Watch logs to ensure locks are properly acquired from both sources\n\n#### Future Deprecation Notice\n\nIn a future minor version of Terraform, DynamoDB-based locking will be deprecated, and you'll need to migrate to S3-native locking or remove the DynamoDB configuration entirely.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks: Keyword Conflict Resolution\n\n#### What Changed\n\nMoved blocks now respect reserved keywords (`local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `data`, `resource`, `terraform`, `variable`, `output`, etc.) when parsing resource addresses.\n\nIf you reference a resource whose type name matches a reserved keyword, you must now prepend `resource.` to the identifier in `moved` blocks.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThis change prevents ambiguous resource references that could be interpreted as variable references or other language constructs. It ensures that moved blocks always reference the resource you intend.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\nThis configuration would work if you had a resource type matching a keyword:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = output.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nYou must now use the `resource.` prefix for any resource type that matches a keyword:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.output.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n#### Resource Types That Require `resource.` Prefix\n\nThe following commonly-used providers have resource types that match reserved keywords:\n\n- `local_file` (type: `local`) - Actually safe, but ensure clarity\n- Custom providers with types named: `data`, `output`, `module`, `resource`, `variable`, `terraform`, `each`, `count`, `self`\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify moved blocks in your configuration** - Search for all `moved` blocks in your configuration\n\n2. **Check resource type names** - For each `moved` block, verify if the resource type name matches any reserved keyword\n\n3. **Identify problematic references** - Run `terraform init` and `terraform plan` to see if any moved blocks produce errors about conflicting keywords\n\n4. **Add `resource.` prefix** - For any problematic references, prepend `resource.` to the resource reference in the `moved` block\n\n5. **Validate the configuration** - Run `terraform validate` to ensure all moved blocks are valid\n\n6. **Test the refactoring** - Apply the configuration to verify the moved blocks work correctly\n\n#### Common Examples\n\n**Example 1: Custom provider with resource type `local`**\n\n```hcl\n# v1.10.0 - If using a custom provider with \"local\" resource type\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n**Example 2: Normal resources (no change needed)**\n\n```hcl\n# These don't need changes - \"aws_instance\" and \"aws_security_group\"\n# don't match reserved keywords\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Not checking all moved blocks** - Search your entire codebase for moved blocks\n- **Forgetting about custom providers** - If you use custom providers, check their resource type names\n- **Applying prefix unnecessarily** - Only add `resource.` if the resource type actually conflicts with a keyword\n- **Ignoring error messages** - If Terraform reports a keyword conflict, add the prefix\n\n---\n\n## Sensitive Value Handling Improvements\n\n### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive marks are propagated in conditional expressions (`if/then/else`) and `for` expressions. In certain cases where v1.9.0 would lose sensitive marks, v1.10.0 preserves them for consistency.\n\n### Key Improvements\n\n1. **Conditional expressions now preserve sensitive marks** from all branches\n2. **For expressions preserve sensitive marks** when the result depends on sensitive inputs\n3. **Unknown values with sensitive marks** are now handled correctly\n4. **Bug fix: Incorrect transfer of sensitive marks** to nested resource values has been corrected\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThese changes typically **improve security** by ensuring sensitive values remain marked throughout evaluation. However, you may see new \"sensitive value\" warnings in outputs that were previously hidden.\n\n### Before (v1.9.0) vs After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\n# Example 1: Conditional expression with sensitive values\nvariable \"password\" {\n  sensitive = true\n  default   = \"secret\"\n}\n\nvariable \"use_custom\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\noutput \"chosen_password\" {\n  # In v1.9.0: This output might NOT be marked sensitive if use_custom is true\n  # In v1.10.0: This output IS marked sensitive because one branch contains sensitive data\n  value = var.use_custom ? \"custom-value\" : var.password\n}\n```\n\n### Migration Steps for Sensitive Value Changes\n\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** and review any new \"sensitive value\" annotations\n2. **Update outputs** - If outputs now show as sensitive and you want them public, use `nonsensitive()`\n3. **Review conditionals** - Check any `if/then/else` expressions that involve sensitive data\n4. **Use `nonsensitive()` carefully** - Only use this function if you've verified the value is safe to expose\n\n### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override\n\n```hcl\n# Example: Extract non-sensitive data from sensitive value\nvariable \"api_response\" {\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\noutput \"status_code\" {\n  # Extract just the status code, which is public information\n  value = nonsensitive(regexall(\"Status: (\\\\d+)\", var.api_response)[0][0])\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Implications\n\n### Ephemeral Values and Resources\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral values as a new capability for handling sensitive data that should not be persisted to state or plan files. This is a significant feature for secret management.\n\n#### What Are Ephemeral Values?\n\nEphemeral values exist only during a Terraform operation and are **not written to state files or plan files**. They're useful for:\n- Short-lived tokens and credentials\n- Temporary secrets from external services\n- Data that's only needed during apply but shouldn't be stored\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral variable\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  # This variable won't be stored in state/plan files\n}\n\n# Use it in a provider configuration\nprovider \"example\" {\n  api_token = var.api_token\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs (in child modules)\n\n```hcl\n# In a child module, define an ephemeral output\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = aws_iam_session_token.example.token\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral resource (provider-dependent)\nephemeral \"vault_generic_secret\" \"database_credentials\" {\n  path = \"secret/data/database\"\n}\n\n# Use it in another resource\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"example\" {\n  master_password = ephemeral.vault_generic_secret.database_credentials.data[\"password\"]\n}\n```\n\n#### Important Restrictions\n\n- Ephemeral values can **only** be referenced in:\n  - Other ephemeral contexts\n  - Provider configurations\n  - Provisioner and connection blocks\n  - Other ephemeral variables/outputs/resources\n\n- **Cannot** be referenced in regular resources or outputs\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\nNew in v1.10.0, use this function to replace ephemeral values with null while preserving non-ephemeral values:\n\n```hcl\n# Convert ephemeral values to null before storing elsewhere\nlocal {\n  safe_for_storage = ephemeralasnull(var.api_token)\n}\n```\n\n#### When to Use Ephemeral Values\n\n- **Provider authentication** - Pass credentials without storing in state\n- **Temporary secrets** - Use short-lived tokens from secret backends\n- **Sensitive defaults** - Provide sensitive default values that shouldn't be persisted\n- **Module outputs** - Return credentials from child modules without state persistence\n\n#### When NOT to Use Ephemeral Values\n\n- Regular resource attributes (use `sensitive = true` instead)\n- Data that needs to persist across `terraform plan` and `terraform apply`\n- State that must be available in other Terraform operations\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Checklist\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n- [ ] Backup your current state file\n- [ ] Review and document all moved blocks in your configuration\n- [ ] Review S3 backend configuration for deprecated attributes\n- [ ] Check for any custom providers with resource type names matching keywords\n- [ ] Test upgrade in a non-production environment first\n\n### Validation Commands\n\n```bash\n# Initialize with the new version\nterraform init\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Plan to identify changes\nterraform plan -out=tfplan\n\n# Review the plan carefully\nterraform show tfplan\n\n# Apply only after reviewing\nterraform apply tfplan\n```\n\n### Key Validation Points\n\n1. **Moved blocks** - Verify no errors about keyword conflicts\n2. **S3 backend** - Confirm IAM role configuration is under the `assume_role` block\n3. **Sensitive values** - Check for any new \"sensitive value\" annotations\n4. **Plan result** - Ensure the plan shows no unexpected resource changes\n\n### Testing Sensitive Value Changes\n\n```bash\n# Run plan and grep for sensitive value indications\nterraform plan | grep -i sensitive\n\n# Compare before/after behavior with specific outputs\nterraform output -raw my_output  # Should fail if marked as sensitive\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If You Need to Rollback\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n1. **Revert your configuration changes** back to v1.9.0 syntax\n2. **Install Terraform v1.9.0**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform version  # Confirm you're on v1.10.0\n   # Download v1.9.0 from https://www.terraform.io/downloads\n   terraform version  # Confirm v1.9.0\n   ```\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** to reinitialize with v1.9.0\n4. **Verify no state changes** with `terraform plan`\n5. **Contact Terraform support** if you identify a bug\n\n### Safe Rollback Strategy\n\n```bash\n# Step 1: Backup current state\ncp terraform.tfstate terraform.tfstate.v110.bak\n\n# Step 2: Revert configuration to v1.9.0 format\ngit checkout main -- *.tf  # or manually revert\n\n# Step 3: Switch to v1.9.0\ntfswitch 1.9.0  # or similar version manager\n\n# Step 4: Initialize with v1.9.0\nterraform init\n\n# Step 5: Verify no unintended changes\nterraform plan\n\n# Step 6: Contact support if plan shows unexpected changes\n```\n\n---\n\n## Specific Migration Examples\n\n### Example 1: Complete S3 Backend Migration\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.9.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                       = \"terraform-state\"\n    key                          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                       = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table               = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-prod\"\n    external_id                  = \"abc123xyz\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-prod\"\n      external_id  = \"abc123xyz\"\n      duration     = 3600\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 2: Ephemeral Variable Usage\n\n```hcl\n# Provider configuration with ephemeral token\nvariable \"vault_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  default   = null\n}\n\nprovider \"vault\" {\n  address = \"https://vault.example.com\"\n  token   = var.vault_token\n}\n\n# Retrieve secrets using the ephemeral provider\ndata \"vault_generic_secret\" \"database\" {\n  path = \"secret/data/database\"\n}\n\n# Use secrets (but they won't be stored in state)\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"example\" {\n  master_username = data.vault_generic_secret.database.data[\"username\"]\n  master_password = data.vault_generic_secret.database.data[\"password\"]\n\n  # Note: These values ARE still stored in state as regular resource attributes\n  # Ephemeral only prevents the variable/data source from being persisted\n}\n```\n\n### Example 3: Moved Block with Keyword\n\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource with type \"local\" (hypothetically)\nresource \"random_pet\" \"pet\" {\n  keepers = {\n    example = \"value\"\n  }\n}\n\n# And previously had:\n# resource \"local\" \"old_name\" { }\n\n# In v1.10.0, update the moved block:\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = random_pet.pet\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Required Actions\n\n### Minimum Required Changes\n\n1. **S3 Backend Users**: Move IAM role attributes inside `assume_role` block\n2. **Moved Block Users**: Add `resource.` prefix if resource type matches keywords\n3. **All Users**: Run `terraform validate` and `terraform plan` before applying\n\n### Recommended Best Practices\n\n1. Use ephemeral variables for provider authentication instead of sensitive variables\n2. Review conditional expressions involving sensitive values\n3. Update bucket policies if enabling S3-native locking\n4. Document ephemeral value usage in module comments\n\n### Timeline for Deprecations\n\n- v1.10.0 (Nov 2024): IAM attributes removed, moved blocks require keyword safety, ephemeral values introduced\n- v1.11+ (Future): DynamoDB locking for S3 backend to be deprecated\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check the official Terraform upgrade guide** - https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/upgrade-guides\n2. **Review error messages** - Terraform provides clear guidance on what changed\n3. **Test in non-production** - Always validate changes before production\n4. **Community forum** - https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core\n5. **GitHub issues** - https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: File Locations and Examples\n\n### Important Configuration Files\n\n- **Backend configuration**: Usually `backend.tf` or in `terraform {}` block of `main.tf`\n- **Moved blocks**: Can be in any `.tf` file, often in a dedicated `moved.tf`\n- **Variables**: Usually `variables.tf` or `variables/*.tf`\n- **Outputs**: Usually `outputs.tf`\n\n### Full Example: Multi-file Migration\n\n**backend.tf:**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**main.tf:**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n  required_providers {\n    aws = {\n      source  = \"hashicorp/aws\"\n      version = \"~> 5.0\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region = \"us-east-1\"\n}\n\nresource \"aws_instance\" \"example\" {\n  ami           = \"ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0\"\n  instance_type = \"t2.micro\"\n}\n```\n\n**moved.tf:**\n```hcl\n# Updated for v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_name\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated**: November 2024\n**Terraform Versions**: v1.9.0 \u2192 v1.10.0\n**Status**: Complete for General Availability\n",

# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Overview

Terraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release that introduces new features for managing ephemeral data and contains important breaking changes that require attention when upgrading.

This guide covers the key breaking changes and new features you need to be aware of when migrating from Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.

### Major Themes

1. **Ephemeral Values and Resources** - New capability to handle sensitive data without persisting it to state
2. **S3 Backend Restructuring** - Removal of deprecated IAM role assumption attributes
3. **Improved Sensitive Value Handling** - Better consistency in mark propagation across conditional expressions
4. **Moved Block Keyword Safety** - Improved resource addressing to avoid conflicts with reserved keywords

---

## Breaking Changes

### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes

#### What Changed

Terraform v1.10.0 removes the following deprecated root-level attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes must now be specified within the `assume_role` block.

| Removed Attribute | New Location |
|---|---|
| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |
| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |
| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |
| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |
| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |
| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |
| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |
| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |

#### Why This Changed

The consolidation into the `assume_role` block provides better organization and makes the configuration structure more consistent with Terraform's block-based syntax patterns.
